B00007FOMP|5.0|Though, many artists of years past, as well as our contemporary musicians, have recorded albums that reflect the turbulence of the times, none conveyed it quite as beautifully as Marvin Gaye's incomparable WHAT'S GOING ON. The lyrics could've been written for our young soldiers in Iraq and Afghanistan (to name a few), on \\"What's Going On (The Ecology)\\" as they were written for those affected by 1971 Vietnam senseless violence and mounting body counts, the pollution that ravaged the oceans and the screaming pain of insufferable global poverty. \\"Save The Children,\\" \\"Wholy Holy\\" and basically every cut are recorded like an intimate parable and musical reflection on the signs of the times. The trials, pain and horrors are documented through seamless percussion, instrumental accompaniment and flawless vocal by Marvin Gaye. The lyrics, alone, carry the weight of this ambitious record. We sense Gaye's urgency to convey (in his own words) God's message to all who listen to the album.<br /><br />In our age, today, where petty tabloid stories, Twitter feeds and publicity stunts set the pace for fame and the measure of success, WHAT'S GOING ON provides us with a sobering reminder of why we all were brought here, to begin with. To bring our own authentic message to the world, even at the cost of being emotional, heart wrenching and even rung out by the pain of revealing our true selves. Marvin Gaye makes that risk more than worth taking. He paves the way to make it possible. That is just how much the songs, here, influenced artists on a global level. It opened the flood gates for creativity, social empowerment and collective thought toward an authentic new canvass of colors.

I give it two stars and not one because it IS a well-made film.  The acting is strong and the director clearly had a vision.<br /><br />Now the bad news.  I find nothing, NOTHING profound or insightful or moving about this film. As another reviewer pointed out, is it really new news that the pursuit of the so-called American dream is shallow and unfulfilling?  Is it really a revelation that if you took a glimpse inside a seemingly perfect American household you'd find a lot of shocking things?  And the solution -- that we should take time to enjoy life and its little moments of beauty ... really?<br /><br />[Note: the following contains some spoilers]<br /><br />Hollywood and the movie-viewing public love movies in which wealthy people are unhappy and can only find happiness by shunning their materialism.  This makes us all feel better:  people who aren't as wealthy as the family portrayed here (which is most of America and most of the movie-watching public) can feel good in knowing that it's OK that they struggle to make ends meet, because, hey, it's better than being rich!  It's the same fake-populist message moviemakers have been throwing at us for decades, and people eat it right up, somehow believing that the family in this movie is \\"just like us.\\"  I doubt that.<br /><br />What's more, again as another reviewer pointed out, this movie should have been titled \\"American White Wealthy Straight Male Fantasy.\\"  This is one of the most misogynistic movies I've seen in years.  Annette Benning should have won the Oscar just for being a good sport in allowing her character to be portrayed in a spectacularly unflattering way.  The ambitious middle-aged career woman is portrayed as a monster, while her daughter is portrayed as more of a female ideal. Why? She falls in love with the boy next door, whom others think is creepy but of course she sees through that and allows him to watch and film her disrobe.  How good of her to enjoy being objectified.  When they agree to run away, she sweetly offers the small amount of money she's saved up.  He smiles protectively and says that's OK, he's made enough money selling drugs to take care of the both of them.  Enlightened viewers are supposed to go along with this and think it's cool and delightfully subversive that he's a drug dealer, and if you have a problem with that you're too morally upright because who is he harming?  Uh, how about all those people who are killed during drug trafficking?  But that's OK, because it's more important that these uptight, angst-ridden American suburbanites are able to cut loose and get high.<br /><br />And then there's the dreadful cliche of the \\"bad guy\\" of the film being a repressed homosexual.  The film wants to show how enlightened and tolerant it is by having a nice gay couple in it and having the Spacey character befriend them.  But including this stereotype subtley suggests that homosexuality is shameful and messes with your head.  I know this was unintentional, but if you're going to make a film that's Oscar-worthy, you can't be that sloppy.<br /><br />I could go on but have gone on too far already, especially since I know all this will fall on deaf ears.  Make a beautiful-looking movie, cast great actors, and make it seem like you're revealing something profound when you're really just slinging the same tired message that is so comforting to audiences -- badaboom badabing, award-winning success.

1416550550|4.0|Kate Morton successfully wrote a book about four generations of English/Australian women.  The book begins in 1913 in a poor attic in London where we meet a little girl on a ship.  This little girl, however, sets sail for Australia without any companionship and she cannot seem to remember her name or anything about herself when asked.  Upon arriving in Australia, a man notices the little girl seemingly abandoned on the wharf and takes her home to care for her until her guardians arrived.  That didn't seem to happen before Nell, the name the Australian family gave to the girl, became part of her new Australian family.<br /><br />Nell had a wonderful life growing up, but on her 21st birthday, her adopted father lets her know that she had been born to other parents.  Nell, who had formerly been easy going and happy, becomes sullen, calls off her engagement, and begins looking for her biological parents.<br /><br />The story again fast forwards over fifty years, and we learn that Nell left to her granddaughter, Cassandra, a small cottage in England.  Cassandra, determined to find out the origins of her grandmother, leaves for England, and the rest of the story follows....<br /><br />Morton does a beautiful job telling three stories at once: 1) the story of Nell's childhood; 2) the story of Nell searching for her ancestry; and 3) Cassandra's search for Nell's biological family.  Morton brings numerous characters to life while writing a book full of suspense, history, romance, and fairy tales.  By skipping back and forth between the present, past and long-past times, Morton never lets the story become boring and always adds a little piece of information that makes the puzzle behind Nell's ancestry come into focus.<br /><br />I gave the book four rather than five stars because I wished that some of the characters did not have such a sad existence.  Nell had a terrible relationship, if any relationship at all, with her daughter and I couldn't tell whether Nell had many happy moments after the realization that she had been adopted.  Cassandra also seems to hold a dark secret from her past and doesn't seem to be happy with her life, except maybe at the very end.  Clearly, Eliza has some happiness in her life, but the end seemed bleak and Rose and Rose's mother only took happiness away from others.y moments after the realization that she had been adopted. B005LAIGOQ|4.0|A young grieving lawyer, Arthur Kipps (Radcliffe) is sent to a remote village to settle the estate of a recently deceased woman who had a quite large English manor. It is very clear from his first arrival that the locals do not want him there, and that they are hiding a terrible secret. As child deaths start to occur in the village, the hatred of the villagers is set against Kipps, and he must, with the help of his friend Sam Daily, seek to unravel out what happened at Eel Marsh House, and who is the woman in black.<br /><br />Based off of a novel of the same name by Susan Hill, and set in the early 1900's England, this unique film was, to me, a very welcome surprise. Out of a very wide genre filled with generic and sometimes pathetic offerings, this one stands out as one of the best horror films I've seen a good while. While keeping the tension, gradually building the dread and at the same time intensifying the mystery, this film is a superb piece of entertaining, thrilling and engaging storytelling. Backed by great acting on Radcliffe's part, (which frankly, I wasn't sure about at first either, he surprised me) and snap directing by Watkins,  the film kept my interest, and kept me in suspense the whole time. It does have its jumping moments, but do not get the idea this is a movie filled with cheap thrills, it is an intelligent and fine example of suspenseful storytelling, one that can be enjoyed by a wide audience.<br /><br />Also, I must comment on the filming of it. The lighting and framing of the shots in this piece was absolutely brilliant. Props to them for building such a great atmosphere throughout the film in that regard.<br /><br />As for content, there's not much to list. When it comes to the disturbing content, I'd say the PG-13 was well earned. The deaths of children occur infrequently throughout the movie and the ghostly woman in black is a quite frightening figure as well. Add in a couple of scenes of extreme tension involving ghosts and it's for sure this is not for the kiddies. There is only perhaps a couple mild profanities, (no more than Sherlock Holmes) and absolutely no sexual content. All in all a pretty clean film.<br /><br />So what's my verdict? As a horror movie fan, I must say four and a half out of five stars. With this level of acting and the brilliant filmmaking, I must give this one a high rating. Not particularly everyone's favorite genre, but this one is well worth it in my opinion.

B000002UC5|5.0|How would you react if you'd just sued the Beatles,who musically defined a generational culture,and effectively broke up the band? Not only that but what if you were one of it's key members too? This is the circumstances Paul McCartney found himself in during 1970. Married to photographer Linda Eastman,the couple were expecting their first child together. Living in McCartney's Scottish country house with with horses and other animals,the couple faced many challenges from Paul's frozen assets to his depression over the whole break up. As John Lennon stated later,the dream was over. Or was it? Ever the optimist McCartney was soon back on his feet looking to rebuild his career. He elected to make a DIY album at home with his own studio equipment. He had a number of songs left over from the final Beatles sessions too that were thus far unused. So perhaps something good could come out of all this chaos.<br /><br />  Right out it's clear this is a very singer/songwriter styled and unadorned album,most songs written on acoustic guitar,organ and drums with few to no overdubs. It's also some to some beautifully crafted songs that actually hold up very well even now. \\"Every Night\\",\\"Junk\\" and even the brief opener \\"That Lovely Linda\\" showcase how Paul had lost nothing in his gift for melody and songcraft. \\"That Would Be Something\\" and the funky \\"Oo You\\" are favorites of mine here,showing his affinity for the blues strongly. There are a several instrumentals here too. The sprightly pop of \\"Valentines Day\\" and \\"Momma Miss America\\" and the more abstract \\"Hot As Sun Glasses\\" and the again very psychedelic blues closer \\"Kreen Akrore\\",one of Paul's darkest compositions ever. Of the Beatle era songs \\"Teddy Boy\\" is a quaint little story song,perhaps about Lennon and \\"Maybe I'm Amazed\\"?Well it's one of Paul's standards and basically an extension from \\"Let It Be\\" with it's epic ballad flavor.<br /><br />  So is this a proper extension of the Beatles output? Not a chance. But it is the beginning of a solo career that at it's core showcased the McCartney could survive and prosper on his own. The Beatles were a bit like a musical brain. In individual parts each had a thing going. But together some unspoken thing got created that gave them a being outside their rock n roll roots. As it turned out each area of this brain did have the capacity to grow into it's own entity. That growth process was only beginning for Paul on this album. He was still running largely on fumes from the freshly dissolved Beatles on this music. And his music hadn't quite fully blossomed into it's own entity yet. Perhaps that's why this album is a very representative image of a debut album to begin with. It has the basic elements of where he came from,boiled down to the bare bones of where he'd be going in the future. And while it's skeletal,almost incomplete sound is a far cry from the type of expansive production McCartney favored at any time in his career this album does lay out an important blueprint for what was to come in the solo career of Paul McCartney.eginning of a solo career that at it's core showcased the McCartney could survive and prosper on his own. It also contains some sharp satire about today's political climate and the US's relations with other countries considered less \\"democratic.\\"<br /><br />Sacha Baron Cohen plays a North African dictator, who finds himself de-throned, and even worse, forced to take a job in a eco-friendly health-food store run by Anna Faris, in order to make ends meet, while he plots to get back in power.  Faris is a walking stereotype of a feminist, but she's also kind of cute, and her company, being hired to cater the event when \\"Aladeen\\" is going to renounce his dictatorship in front of many world leaders (all eager to partake of his country`s petroleum products), is a perfect cover to sneak in.  On the way there, he'll learn some life lessons about what's important in life, what qualities make up the perfect life partner, and what not to carry when being transported into a hotel room.<br /><br />The movie's humor level is uneven, which is a disappointment.  When it's funny, it's very, very funny; when it's not and the joke is drawn out too long, it makes you check your watch.  The outtakes are amusing, though.  Unlike \\"Borat\\" or \\"Bruno,\\" there are no celebrities getting \\"punked,;\\" all the actors, who do a decent job, are in on the jokes.

It was released in 1955.<br /> The story:<br />Handsome drifter Hal Carter (William Holden) hops off the boxcar into a dusty little Kansas town to connect with old college buddy, wealthy Alan Benson (Cliff Robertson).<br />Benson's father owns a lucrative grain elevator business and Hal desperately needs a job.
